(opencontainers/runc)</summary>\n\n### [`v1.1.12`](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/releases/tag/v1.1.12): runc 1.1.12 -- &quot;Now you&#x27;re thinking with Portals™!&quot;\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/compare/v1.1.11...v1.1.12)\n\nThis is the twelfth patch release in the 1.1.z release branch of runc.\nIt fixes a high-severity container breakout vulnerability involving\nleaked file descriptors, and users are strongly encouraged to update as\nsoon as possible.\n\n-   Fix [CVE-2024-21626][cve-2024-21626], a container breakout attack that took advantage of\n    a file descriptor that was leaked internally within runc (but never\n    leaked to the container process).\n\n    In addition to fixing the leak, several strict hardening measures were\n    added to ensure that future internal leaks could not be used to break\n    out in this manner again.\n\n    Based on our research, while no other container runtime had a similar\n    leak, none had any of the hardening steps we've introduced (and some\n    runtimes would not check for any file descriptors that a calling\n    process may have leaked to them, allowing for container breakouts due\n    to basic user error).\n\n##### Static Linking Notices\n\nThe `runc` binary distributed with this release are *statically linked* with\nthe following [GNU LGPL-2.1][lgpl-2.1] licensed libraries, with `runc` acting\nas a \"work that uses the Library\":\n\n[lgpl-2.1]: https://www.gnu.org/licenses/old-licenses/lgpl-2.1.en.html\n\n-   [libseccomp](https://togithub.com/seccomp/libseccomp)\n\nThe versions of these libraries were not modified from their upstream versions,\nbut in order to comply with the LGPL-2.1 (§6(a)), we have attached the\ncomplete source code for those libraries which (when combined with the attached\nrunc source code) may be used to exercise your rights under the LGPL-2.1.\n\nHowever we strongly suggest that you make use of your distribution's packages\nor download them from the authoritative upstream sources, especially since\nthese libraries are related to the security of your containers.\n\n<hr/>\n\nThanks to all of the contributors who made this release possible:\n\n-   Aleksa Sarai <cyphar@cyphar.com>\n-   hang.jiang <hang.jiang@daocloud.io>\n-   lfbzhm <lifubang@acmcoder.com>\n\n[cve-2024-21626]: https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/security/advisories/GHSA-xr7r-f8xq-vfvv\n\nSigned-off-by: Aleksa Sarai <cyphar@cyphar.com>\n\n### [`v1.1.11`](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/releases/tag/v1.1.11): runc 1.1.11 -- &quot;Happy New Year!&quot;\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/compare/v1.1.10...v1.1.11)\n\nThis is the eleventh patch release in the 1.1.z release branch of runc.\nIt primarily fixes a few issues with runc's handling of containers that\nare configured to join existing user namespaces, as well as improvements\nto cgroupv2 support.\n\n-   Fix several issues with userns path handling. ([#&#8203;4122](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4122), [#&#8203;4124](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4124), [#&#8203;4134](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4134), [#&#8203;4144](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4144))\n-   Support memory.peak and memory.swap.peak in cgroups v2.\n    Add `swapOnlyUsage` in `MemoryStats`. This field reports swap-only usage.\n    For cgroupv1, `Usage` and `Failcnt` are set by subtracting memory usage\n    from memory+swap usage. For cgroupv2, `Usage`, `Limit`, and `MaxUsage`\n    are set. ([#&#8203;4000](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4000), [#&#8203;4010](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4010), [#&#8203;4131](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4131))\n-   build(deps): bump github.com/cyphar/filepath-securejoin. ([#&#8203;4140](https://togithub.com/opencontainers/runc/issues/4140))\n\n##### Static Linking Notices\n\nThe `runc` binary distributed with this release are *statically linked* with\nthe following [GNU LGPL-2.1][lgpl-2.1] licensed libraries, with `runc` acting\nas a \"work that uses the Library\":\n\n[lgpl-2.1]: https://www.gnu.org/licenses/old-licenses/lgpl-2.1.en.html\n\n-   [libseccomp](https://togithub.com/seccomp/libseccomp)\n\nThe versions of these libraries were not modified from their upstream versions,\nbut in order to comply with the LGPL-2.1 (§6(a)), we have attached the\ncomplete source code for those libraries which (when combined with the attached\nrunc source code) may be used to exercise your rights under the LGPL-2.1.\n\nHowever we strongly suggest that you make use of your distribution's packages\nor download them from the authoritative upstream sources, especially since\nthese libraries are related to the security of your containers.\n\n<hr/>\n\nThanks to all of the contributors who made this release possible:\n\n-   Aleksa Sarai <cyphar@cyphar.com>\n-   Heran Yang <heran55@&#8203;126.com>\n-   Kir Kolyshkin Full details are in the issue ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526)) and bug fix ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571)).  There's also a developer's [bug summary](https://gist.github.com/rincebrain/e23b4a39aba3fadc04db18574d30dc73) that gives a good overview.  We recommend everyone either upgrade to 2.2.2 or 2.1.14 to get the fix.  The bug can cause data corruption due to an incorrect dirty dnode check.  This bug is very hard to hit, and really only came to light due to changes in `cp` in coreutils 9.x.  It's extremely unlikely that the bug was ever hit on EL7 or EL8, when running `cp` since they all use coreutils 8.x which performs file copies differently.\n\n*Updated (12/1/23):*\nEL9 was previously vulnerable since it uses coreutils 8.32 with the SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE patches backported from coreutils 9.x.\n\n-   FreeBSD: Fix ZFS so that snapshots under .zfs/snapshot are NFS visible [`v2.2.1`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/releases/tag/zfs-2.2.1)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/compare/zfs-2.2.0...zfs-2.2.1)\n\n##### Supported Platforms\n\n-   **Linux**: this release. To workaround this, zfs-2.2.1 disables block cloning by default (see [https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15529](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15529) and [`479dca5`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/commit/479dca51c66a731e637bd2d4f9bba01a05f9ac9f)). Users running the 2.1.x branch or older are unaffected, as block cloning is a 2.2.x-only feature.\n\n-   ZTS: Fix 'could not unmount datasets' on Alma 9 ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15542](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15542))\n-   zfs-2.2.1: Disable block cloning by default ([`479dca5`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/commit/479dca51c66a731e637bd2d4f9bba01a05f9ac9f))\n-   Add a tunable to disable BRT support. [#&#8203;15405](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15405)\n-   Fix ZED auto-replace for VDEVs using by-id paths [#&#8203;15363](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15363)\n-   Add zfs_prepare_disk script for disk firmware install [#&#8203;15243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15243)\n-   Large sync writes perform worse with slog [#&#8203;14378](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14378)\n-   FreeBSD: Improve taskq wrapper [#&#8203;15356](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15356)\n-   Fix block cloning between unencrypted and encrypted datasets [#&#8203;15464](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15464) [#&#8203;15465](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15465)\n\n### [`v2.2.0`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/releases/tag/zfs-2.2.0)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/compare/zfs-2.1.14...zfs-2.2.0)\n\n##### Supported Platforms\n\n-   **Linux**: compatible with 3.10 - 6.5 kernels\n-   **FreeBSD**: compatible with releases starting from 12.2-RELEASE\n\n##### New Features\n\n-   **Block cloning** ([#&#8203;13392](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13392)) - Block cloning is a facility that allows a file (or parts of a file) to be \"cloned\", that is, a shallow copy made where the existing data blocks are referenced rather than copied.  Later modifications to the data will cause a copy of the data block to be taken and that copy modified.  This facility is used to implement \"reflinks\" or \"file-level copy-on-write\".  Many common file copying programs, including newer versions of `/bin/cp` on Linux, will try to create clones automatically.\n\n-   **Linux container support** ([#&#8203;12209](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12209), [#&#8203;14070](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14070), [#&#8203;14097](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14097), [#&#8203;12263](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12263)) - Added support for Linux-specific container interfaces such as `renameat(2)`, support for overlayfs, idmapped mounts in a user namespace, and namespace delegation support for containers.\n\n-   **Scrub error log** ([#&#8203;12812](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12812), [#&#8203;12355](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12355)) - `zpool status` will report all filesystems, snapshots, and clones affected by a shared corrupt block.  `zpool scrub -e` can be used to scrub only the known damaged blocks in the error log to perform a fast, targeted repair when possible.\n\n-   **BLAKE3 checksums** ([#&#8203;12918](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12918)) - [BLAKE3](https://togithub.com/BLAKE3-team/BLAKE3) is a modern cryptographic hash algorithm focused on high performance.  It is much faster than sha256, sha512, and can be up 3x faster than Edon-R.  BLAKE3 is the recommended secure checksum.\n\n-   **Corrective \"zfs receive\"** ([#&#8203;9372](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/9372)) - A new type of `zfs receive` which can be used to heal corrupted data in filesystems, snapshots, and clones when a replica of the data already exists in the form of a backup send stream.\n\n-   **Vdev properties** ([#&#8203;11711](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11711)) - Provides observability of individual vdevs in a programmatic way.\n\n-   **Vdev and zpool user properties** ([#&#8203;11680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11680)) - Lets you set custom user properties on vdevs and zpools, similar to the existing zfs dataset user properties.\n\n##### Performance\n\n-   **Fully adaptive ARC** ([#&#8203;14359](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14359)) - A unified ARC which relaxes the artificial limits imposed by both the MRU/MFU distribution and data/metadata distinction.  This allows the ARC to better adjust to highly dynamic workloads and minimizes the need for manual workload-dependent tuning.\n\n-   **SHA2 checksums** ([#&#8203;13741](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13741)) - Optimized SHA2 checksum implementation to use hardware acceleration when available.\n\n-   **Edon-R checksums** ([#&#8203;13618](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13618)) - Reworked the Edon-R variants and optimized the code to make several minor speed ups.\n\n-   **ZSTD early abort** ([#&#8203;13244](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13244)) - When using the zstd compression algorithm, data that can not be compressed is detected quickly, avoiding wasted work.\n\n-   **Prefetch improvements** ([#&#8203;14603](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14603), [#&#8203;14516](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14516), [#&#8203;14402](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14402), [#&#8203;14243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14243), [#&#8203;13452](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13452)) - Extensive I/O prefetching analysis and optimization.\n\n-   **General optimization** ([#&#8203;14121](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14121), [#&#8203;14123](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14123), [#&#8203;14039](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14039), [#&#8203;13680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13680), [#&#8203;13613](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13613), [#&#8203;13606](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13606), [#&#8203;13576](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13576), [#&#8203;13553](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13553), [#&#8203;12789](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12789), [#&#8203;14925](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14925), [#&#8203;14948](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14948)) - Numerous performance improvements throughout.\n\n##### Additional Information\n\n-   **Documentation** - [OpenZFS documentation](https://openzfs.github.io/openzfs-docs/) for Linux and FreeBSD.\n\n-   **Change log** - The API and ABI are still backward compatible with liblzma\n        5.4.x and 5.2.x and 5.0.x.\n\n        NOTE: As described in the NEWS for 5.5.2beta, the core components\n        are now under the BSD Zero Clause License (0BSD).\n\n        Since 5.5.2beta:\n\n        * liblzma:\n\n            - Disabled the branchless C variant in the LZMA decoder based\n              on the benchmark results from the community.\n\n            - Disabled x86-64 inline assembly on x32 to fix the build.\n\n        * Sandboxing support in xz:\n\n            - Landlock is now used even when xz needs to create files.\n              In this case the sandbox is has to be more permissive than\n              when no files need to be created. A similar thing was\n              already in use with pledge(2) since 5.3.4alpha.\n\n            - Landlock and pledge(2) are now stricter when reading from\n              more than one input file and only writing to standard output.\n\n            - Added support for Landlock ABI version 4.\n\n        * CMake:\n\n            - Default to -O2 instead of -O3 with CMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release.\n              -O3 is not useful for speed and makes the code larger.\n\n            - Now builds lzmainfo and lzmadec.\n\n            - xzdiff, xzgrep, xzless, xzmore, and their symlinks are now\n              installed. The scripts are also tested during \"make test\".\n\n            - Added translation support for xz, lzmainfo, and the\n              man pages.\n\n            - Applied the symbol versioning workaround for MicroBlaze that\n              is used in the Autotools build.\n\n            - The general XZ Utils and liblzma API documentation is now\n              installed.\n\n            - The CMake component names were changed a little and several\n              were added. liblzma_Runtime and liblzma_Development are\n              unchanged.\n\n            - Minimum required CMake version is now 3.14. However,\n              translation support is disabled with CMake versions\n              older than 3.20.\n\n            - The CMake-based build is now close to feature parity with the\n              Autotools-based build. Most importantly a few tests aren't\n              run yet. Testing the CMake-based build on different operating\n              systems would be welcome now. See the comment at the top of\n              CMakeLists.txt.\n\n        * Fixed a bug in the Autotools feature test for ARM64 CRC32\n          instruction support for old versions of Clang. This did not\n          affect the CMake build.\n\n        * Windows:\n\n            - The build instructions in INSTALL and windows/INSTALL*.txt\n              were revised completely.\n\n            - windows/build-with-cmake.bat along with the instructions\n              in windows/INSTALL-MinGW-w64_with_CMake.txt should make\n              it very easy to build liblzma.dll and xz.exe on Windows\n              using CMake and MinGW-w64 with either GCC or Clang/LLVM.\n\n            - windows/build.bash was updated. It now works on MSYS2 and\n              on GNU/Linux (cross-compiling) to create a .zip and .7z\n              package for 32-bit and 64-bit x86 using GCC + MinGW-w64.\n\n        * The TODO file is no longer installed as part of the\n          documentation. The file is out of date and does not reflect\n          the actual tasks that will be completed in the future.\n\n        * Translations:\n\n            - Translated lzmainfo man pages are now installed. These\n              had been forgotten in earlier versions.\n\n            - Updated Croatian, Esperanto, German, Hungarian, Korean,\n              Polish, Romanian, Spanish, Swedish, Vietnamese, and Ukrainian\n              translations.\n\n            - Updated German, Korean, Romanian, and Ukrainian man page\n              translations.\n\n        * Added a few tests.\n\n</details>\n\n<details>\n<summary>u-boot/u-boot (u-boot/u-boot)</summary>\n\n### [`v2023.10-rc1`](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2023.10-rc2...v2023.10-rc1)\n\n[Compare Full details are in the issue ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526)) and bug fix ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571)).  There's also a developer's [bug summary](https://gist.github.com/rincebrain/e23b4a39aba3fadc04db18574d30dc73) that gives a good overview.  We recommend everyone either upgrade to 2.2.2 or 2.1.14 to get the fix.  The bug can cause data corruption due to an incorrect dirty dnode check.  This bug is very hard to hit, and really only came to light due to changes in `cp` in coreutils 9.x.  It's extremely unlikely that the bug was ever hit on EL7 or EL8, when running `cp` since they all use coreutils 8.x which performs file copies differently.\n\n*Updated (12/1/23):*\nEL9 was previously vulnerable since it uses coreutils 8.32 with the SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE patches backported from coreutils 9.x.\n\n-   FreeBSD: Fix ZFS so that snapshots under .zfs/snapshot are NFS visible [#&#8203;15405](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15405)\n-   Fix ZED auto-replace for VDEVs using by-id paths [#&#8203;15363](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15363)\n-   Add zfs_prepare_disk script for disk firmware install [#&#8203;15243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15243)\n-   Large sync writes perform worse with slog [#&#8203;14378](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14378)\n-   FreeBSD: Improve taskq wrapper [#&#8203;15356](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15356)\n-   Fix block cloning between unencrypted and encrypted datasets [#&#8203;15464](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15464) [#&#8203;15465](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15465)\n\n### [`v2.2.0`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/releases/tag/zfs-2.2.0)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/compare/zfs-2.1.14...zfs-2.2.0)\n\n##### Supported Platforms\n\n-   **Linux**: compatible with 3.10 - 6.5 kernels\n-   **FreeBSD**: compatible with releases starting from 12.2-RELEASE\n\n##### New Features\n\n-   **Block cloning** ([#&#8203;13392](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13392)) - Block cloning is a facility that allows a file (or parts of a file) to be \"cloned\", that is, a shallow copy made where the existing data blocks are referenced rather than copied.  Later modifications to the data will cause a copy of the data block to be taken and that copy modified.  This facility is used to implement \"reflinks\" or \"file-level copy-on-write\".  Many common file copying programs, including newer versions of `/bin/cp` on Linux, will try to create clones automatically.\n\n-   **Linux container support** ([#&#8203;12209](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12209), [#&#8203;14070](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14070), [#&#8203;14097](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14097), [#&#8203;12263](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12263)) - Added support for Linux-specific container interfaces such as `renameat(2)`, support for overlayfs, idmapped mounts in a user namespace, and namespace delegation support for containers.\n\n-   **Scrub error log** ([#&#8203;12812](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12812), [#&#8203;12355](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12355)) - `zpool status` will report all filesystems, snapshots, and clones affected by a shared corrupt block.  `zpool scrub -e` can be used to scrub only the known damaged blocks in the error log to perform a fast, targeted repair when possible.\n\n-   **BLAKE3 checksums** ([#&#8203;12918](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12918)) - [BLAKE3](https://togithub.com/BLAKE3-team/BLAKE3) is a modern cryptographic hash algorithm focused on high performance.  It is much faster than sha256, sha512, and can be up 3x faster than Edon-R.  BLAKE3 is the recommended secure checksum.\n\n-   **Corrective \"zfs receive\"** ([#&#8203;9372](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/9372)) - A new type of `zfs receive` which can be used to heal corrupted data in filesystems, snapshots, and clones when a replica of the data already exists in the form of a backup send stream.\n\n-   **Vdev properties** ([#&#8203;11711](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11711)) - Provides observability of individual vdevs in a programmatic way.\n\n-   **Vdev and zpool user properties** ([#&#8203;11680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11680)) - Lets you set custom user properties on vdevs and zpools, similar to the existing zfs dataset user properties.\n\n##### Performance\n\n-   **Fully adaptive ARC** ([#&#8203;14359](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14359)) - A unified ARC which relaxes the artificial limits imposed by both the MRU/MFU distribution and data/metadata distinction.  This allows the ARC to better adjust to highly dynamic workloads and minimizes the need for manual workload-dependent tuning.\n\n-   **SHA2 checksums** ([#&#8203;13741](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13741)) - Optimized SHA2 checksum implementation to use hardware acceleration when available.\n\n-   **Edon-R checksums** ([#&#8203;13618](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13618)) - Reworked the Edon-R variants and optimized the code to make several minor speed ups.\n\n-   **ZSTD early abort** ([#&#8203;13244](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13244)) - When using the zstd compression algorithm, data that can not be compressed is detected quickly, avoiding wasted work.\n\n-   **Prefetch improvements** ([#&#8203;14603](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14603), [#&#8203;14516](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14516), [#&#8203;14402](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14402), [#&#8203;14243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14243), [#&#8203;13452](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13452)) - Extensive I/O prefetching analysis and optimization.\n\n-   **General optimization** ([#&#8203;14121](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14121), [#&#8203;14123](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14123), [#&#8203;14039](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14039), [#&#8203;13680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13680), [#&#8203;13613](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13613), [#&#8203;13606](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13606), [#&#8203;13576](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13576), [#&#8203;13553](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13553), [#&#8203;12789](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12789), [#&#8203;14925](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14925), [#&#8203;14948](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14948)) - Numerous performance improvements throughout.\n\n##### Additional Information\n\n-   **Documentation** - [OpenZFS documentation](https://openzfs.github.io/openzfs-docs/) for Linux and FreeBSD.\n\n-   **Change log** - [`v5.6.0`](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/releases/tag/v5.6.0): XZ Utils 5.6.0 Stable\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/compare/v5.4.6...v5.6.0)\n\nThere currently are no plans to maintain the 5.4.x branch, but releases\ncould be made if there is community interest.\n\nHere is an extract from the NEWS file:\n\n    5.6.0 (2024-02-24)\n\n        This bumps the minor version of liblzma because new features were\n        added. The API and ABI are still backward compatible with liblzma\n        5.4.x and 5.2.x and 5.0.x.\n\n        NOTE: As described in the NEWS for 5.5.2beta, the core components\n        are now under the BSD Zero Clause License (0BSD).\n\n        Since 5.5.2beta:\n\n        * liblzma:\n\n            - Disabled the branchless C variant in the LZMA decoder based\n              on the benchmark results from the community.\n\n            - Disabled x86-64 inline assembly on x32 to fix the build.\n\n        * Sandboxing support in xz:\n\n            - Landlock is now used even when xz needs to create files.\n              In this case the sandbox is has to be more permissive than\n              when no files need to be created. A similar thing was\n              already in use with pledge(2) since 5.3.4alpha.\n\n            - Landlock and pledge(2) are now stricter when reading from\n              more than one input file and only writing to standard output.\n\n            - Added support for Landlock ABI version 4.\n\n        * CMake:\n\n            - Default to -O2 instead of -O3 with CMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release.\n              -O3 is not useful for speed and makes the code larger.\n\n            - Now builds lzmainfo and lzmadec.\n\n            - xzdiff, xzgrep, xzless, xzmore, and their symlinks are now\n              installed. The scripts are also tested during \"make test\".\n\n            - Added translation support for xz, lzmainfo, and the\n              man pages.\n\n            - Applied the symbol versioning workaround for MicroBlaze that\n              is used in the Autotools build.\n\n            - The general XZ Utils and liblzma API documentation is now\n              installed.\n\n            - The CMake component names were changed a little and several\n              were added. liblzma_Runtime and liblzma_Development are\n              unchanged.\n\n            - Minimum required CMake version is now 3.14. However,\n              translation support is disabled with CMake versions\n              older than 3.20.\n\n            - The CMake-based build is now close to feature parity with the\n              Autotools-based build. Most importantly a few tests aren't\n              run yet. Testing the CMake-based build on different operating\n              systems would be welcome now. See the comment at the top of\n              CMakeLists.txt.\n\n        * Fixed a bug in the Autotools feature test for ARM64 CRC32\n          instruction support for old versions of Clang. This did not\n          affect the CMake build.\n\n        * Windows:\n\n            - The build instructions in INSTALL and windows/INSTALL*.txt\n              were revised completely.\n\n            - windows/build-with-cmake.bat along with the instructions\n              in windows/INSTALL-MinGW-w64_with_CMake.txt should make\n              it very easy to build liblzma.dll and xz.exe on Windows\n              using CMake and MinGW-w64 with either GCC or Clang/LLVM.\n\n            - windows/build.bash was updated. It now works on MSYS2 and\n              on GNU/Linux (cross-compiling) to create a .zip and .7z\n              package for 32-bit and 64-bit x86 using GCC + MinGW-w64.\n\n        * The TODO file is no longer installed as part of the\n          documentation. The file is out of date and does not reflect\n          the actual tasks that will be completed in the future.\n\n        * Translations:\n\n            - Translated lzmainfo man pages are now installed. These\n              had been forgotten in earlier versions.\n\n            - Updated Croatian, Esperanto, German, Hungarian, Korean,\n              Polish, Romanian, Spanish, Swedish, Vietnamese, and Ukrainian\n              translations.\n\n            - Updated German, Korean, Romanian, and Ukrainian man page\n              translations.\n\n        * Added a few tests.\n\n### [`v5.4.6`](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/releases/tag/v5.4.6): XZ Utils 5.4.6 Stable\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/compare/v5.4.5...v5.4.6)\n\nHere is an extract from the NEWS file:\n\n    5.4.6 (2024-01-26)\n\n        * Fixed a bug involving internal function pointers in liblzma not\n          being initialized to NULL. The bug can only be triggered if\n          lzma_filters_update() is called on a LZMA1 encoder, so it does\n          not affect xz or any application known to us that uses liblzma.\n\n        * xz:\n\n            - Fixed a regression introduced in 5.4.2 that caused encoding\n              in the raw format to unnecessarily fail if --suffix was not\n              used. For instance, the following command no longer reports\n              that --suffix must be used:\n\n                  echo foo | xz --format=raw --lzma2 | wc -c\n\n            - Fixed an issue on MinGW-w64 builds that prevented reading\n              from or writing to non-terminal character devices like NUL.\n\n        * Added a new test.\n\n</details>\n\n---\n\n### Configuration\n\n📅 **Schedule**: Branch creation - At any time (no schedule defined), Automerge - At any time (no schedule defined).\n\n🚦 **Automerge**: Disabled by config. Full details are in the issue ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526)) and bug fix ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571)).  There's also a developer's [bug summary](https://gist.github.com/rincebrain/e23b4a39aba3fadc04db18574d30dc73) that gives a good overview.  We recommend everyone either upgrade to 2.2.2 or 2.1.14 to get the fix.  The bug can cause data corruption due to an incorrect dirty dnode check.  This bug is very hard to hit, and really only came to light due to changes in `cp` in coreutils 9.x.  It's extremely unlikely that the bug was ever hit on EL7 or EL8, when running `cp` since they all use coreutils 8.x which performs file copies differently.\n\n*Updated (12/1/23):*\nEL9 was previously vulnerable since it uses coreutils 8.32 with the SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE patches backported from coreutils 9.x.\n\n-   FreeBSD: Fix ZFS so that snapshots under .zfs/snapshot are NFS visible [`v2.2.1`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/releases/tag/zfs-2.2.1)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/compare/zfs-2.2.0...zfs-2.2.1)\n\n##### Supported Platforms\n\n-   **Linux**: compatible with 3.10 - 6.6 kernels\n-   **FreeBSD**: compatible with releases starting from 12.2-RELEASE\n\n##### Changes\n\n**Note**:  We recommend that anyone running zfs-2.2.0 to please update to this release.  Gentoo users have identified a block cloning bug ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526)) that can result in data corruption in zfs-2.2.0.  To workaround this, zfs-2.2.1 disables block cloning by default (see [https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15529](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15529) and [`479dca5`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/commit/479dca51c66a731e637bd2d4f9bba01a05f9ac9f)). Users running the 2.1.x branch or older are unaffected, as block cloning is a 2.2.x-only feature.\n\n-   ZTS: Fix 'could not unmount datasets' on Alma 9 ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15542](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15542))\n-   zfs-2.2.1: Disable block cloning by default ([`479dca5`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/commit/479dca51c66a731e637bd2d4f9bba01a05f9ac9f))\n-   Add a tunable to disable BRT support. [#&#8203;15427](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15427)\n-   Trust ARC_BUF_SHARED() more [#&#8203;15397](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15397)\n-   Remove lock from dsl_pool_need_dirty_delay() [#&#8203;15390](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15390)\n-   run-zts test procfs/pool_state failed with uncorrectable I/O failure [#&#8203;15364](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15364)\n-   Properly pad struct tx_cpu to cache line [#&#8203;15402](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15402)\n-   Fix typo in  tests/zfs-tests/tests/functional/cli_user/misc/misc.cfg [#&#8203;15417](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15417)\n-   FreeBSD: taskq: Remove unused declaration [#&#8203;15416](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15416)\n-   Set spa_ccw_fail_time=0 when expanding a vdev. [#&#8203;15405](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15405)\n-   Fix ZED auto-replace for VDEVs using by-id paths [#&#8203;15363](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15363)\n-   Add zfs_prepare_disk script for disk firmware install [#&#8203;15243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15243)\n-   Large sync writes perform worse with slog [#&#8203;14378](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14378)\n-   FreeBSD: Improve taskq wrapper [#&#8203;15356](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15356)\n-   Fix block cloning between unencrypted and encrypted datasets [#&#8203;15464](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15464) [#&#8203;15465](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15465)\n\n### [`v2.2.0`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/releases/tag/zfs-2.2.0)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/compare/zfs-2.1.14...zfs-2.2.0)\n\n##### Supported Platforms\n\n-   **Linux**: compatible with 3.10 - 6.5 kernels\n-   **FreeBSD**: compatible with releases starting from 12.2-RELEASE\n\n##### New Features\n\n-   **Block cloning** ([#&#8203;13392](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13392)) - Block cloning is a facility that allows a file (or parts of a file) to be \"cloned\", that is, a shallow copy made where the existing data blocks are referenced rather than copied.  Later modifications to the data will cause a copy of the data block to be taken and that copy modified.  This facility is used to implement \"reflinks\" or \"file-level copy-on-write\".  Many common file copying programs, including newer versions of `/bin/cp` on Linux, will try to create clones automatically.\n\n-   **Linux container support** ([#&#8203;12209](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12209), [#&#8203;14070](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14070), [#&#8203;14097](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14097), [#&#8203;12263](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12263)) - Added support for Linux-specific container interfaces such as `renameat(2)`, support for overlayfs, idmapped mounts in a user namespace, and namespace delegation support for containers.\n\n-   **Scrub error log** ([#&#8203;12812](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12812), [#&#8203;12355](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12355)) - `zpool status` will report all filesystems, snapshots, and clones affected by a shared corrupt block.  `zpool scrub -e` can be used to scrub only the known damaged blocks in the error log to perform a fast, targeted repair when possible.\n\n-   **BLAKE3 checksums** ([#&#8203;12918](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12918)) - [BLAKE3](https://togithub.com/BLAKE3-team/BLAKE3) is a modern cryptographic hash algorithm focused on high performance.  It is much faster than sha256, sha512, and can be up 3x faster than Edon-R.  BLAKE3 is the recommended secure checksum.\n\n-   **Corrective \"zfs receive\"** ([#&#8203;9372](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/9372)) - A new type of `zfs receive` which can be used to heal corrupted data in filesystems, snapshots, and clones when a replica of the data already exists in the form of a backup send stream.\n\n-   **Vdev properties** ([#&#8203;11711](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11711)) - Provides observability of individual vdevs in a programmatic way.\n\n-   **Vdev and zpool user properties** ([#&#8203;11680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11680)) - Lets you set custom user properties on vdevs and zpools, similar to the existing zfs dataset user properties.\n\n##### Performance\n\n-   **Fully adaptive ARC** ([#&#8203;14359](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14359)) - A unified ARC which relaxes the artificial limits imposed by both the MRU/MFU distribution and data/metadata distinction.  This allows the ARC to better adjust to highly dynamic workloads and minimizes the need for manual workload-dependent tuning.\n\n-   **SHA2 checksums** ([#&#8203;13741](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13741)) - Optimized SHA2 checksum implementation to use hardware acceleration when available.\n\n-   **Edon-R checksums** ([#&#8203;13618](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13618)) - Reworked the Edon-R variants and optimized the code to make several minor speed ups.\n\n-   **ZSTD early abort** ([#&#8203;13244](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13244)) - When using the zstd compression algorithm, data that can not be compressed is detected quickly, avoiding wasted work.\n\n-   **Prefetch improvements** ([#&#8203;14603](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14603), [#&#8203;14516](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14516), [#&#8203;14402](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14402), [#&#8203;14243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14243), [#&#8203;13452](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13452)) - Extensive I/O prefetching analysis and optimization.\n\n-   **General optimization** ([#&#8203;14121](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14121), [#&#8203;14123](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14123), [#&#8203;14039](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14039), [#&#8203;13680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13680), [#&#8203;13613](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13613), [#&#8203;13606](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13606), [#&#8203;13576](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13576), [#&#8203;13553](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13553), [#&#8203;12789](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12789), [#&#8203;14925](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14925), [#&#8203;14948](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14948)) - Numerous performance improvements throughout.\n\n##### Additional Information\n\n-   **Documentation** - [OpenZFS documentation](https://openzfs.github.io/openzfs-docs/) for Linux and FreeBSD.\n\n-   **Change log** - [`v5.6.0`](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/releases/tag/v5.6.0): XZ Utils 5.6.0 Stable\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/compare/v5.4.6...v5.6.0)\n\nThere currently are no plans to maintain the 5.4.x branch, but releases\ncould be made if there is community interest.\n\nHere is an extract from the NEWS file:\n\n    5.6.0 (2024-02-24)\n\n        This bumps the minor version of liblzma because new features were\n        added. The API and ABI are still backward compatible with liblzma\n        5.4.x and 5.2.x and 5.0.x.\n\n        NOTE: As described in the NEWS for 5.5.2beta, the core components\n        are now under the BSD Zero Clause License (0BSD).\n\n        Since 5.5.2beta:\n\n        * liblzma:\n\n            - Disabled the branchless C variant in the LZMA decoder based\n              on the benchmark results from the community.\n\n            - Disabled x86-64 inline assembly on x32 to fix the build.\n\n        * Sandboxing support in xz:\n\n            - Landlock is now used even when xz needs to create files.\n              In this case the sandbox is has to be more permissive than\n              when no files need to be created. A similar thing was\n              already in use with pledge(2) since 5.3.4alpha.\n\n            - Landlock and pledge(2) are now stricter when reading from\n              more than one input file and only writing to standard output.\n\n            - Added support for Landlock ABI version 4.\n\n        * CMake:\n\n            - Default to -O2 instead of -O3 with CMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release.\n              -O3 is not useful for speed and makes the code larger.\n\n            - Now builds lzmainfo and lzmadec.\n\n            - xzdiff, xzgrep, xzless, xzmore, and their symlinks are now\n              installed. The scripts are also tested during \"make test\".\n\n            - Added translation support for xz, lzmainfo, and the\n              man pages.\n\n            - Applied the symbol versioning workaround for MicroBlaze that\n              is used in the Autotools build.\n\n            - The general XZ Utils and liblzma API documentation is now\n              installed.\n\n            - The CMake component names were changed a little and several\n              were added. liblzma_Runtime and liblzma_Development are\n              unchanged.\n\n            - Minimum required CMake version is now 3.14. However,\n              translation support is disabled with CMake versions\n              older than 3.20.\n\n            - The CMake-based build is now close to feature parity with the\n              Autotools-based build. Most importantly a few tests aren't\n              run yet. Testing the CMake-based build on different operating\n              systems would be welcome now. See the comment at the top of\n              CMakeLists.txt.\n\n        * Fixed a bug in the Autotools feature test for ARM64 CRC32\n          instruction support for old versions of Clang. This did not\n          affect the CMake build.\n\n        * Windows:\n\n            - The build instructions in INSTALL and windows/INSTALL*.txt\n              were revised completely.\n\n            - windows/build-with-cmake.bat along with the instructions\n              in windows/INSTALL-MinGW-w64_with_CMake.txt should make\n              it very easy to build liblzma.dll and xz.exe on Windows\n              using CMake and MinGW-w64 with either GCC or Clang/LLVM.\n\n            - windows/build.bash was updated. It now works on MSYS2 and\n              on GNU/Linux (cross-compiling) to create a .zip and .7z\n              package for 32-bit and 64-bit x86 using GCC + MinGW-w64.\n\n        * The TODO file is no longer installed as part of the\n          documentation. The file is out of date and does not reflect\n          the actual tasks that will be completed in the future.\n\n        * Translations:\n\n            - Translated lzmainfo man pages are now installed. These\n              had been forgotten in earlier versions.\n\n            - Updated Croatian, Esperanto, German, Hungarian, Korean,\n              Polish, Romanian, Spanish, Swedish, Vietnamese, and Ukrainian\n              translations.\n\n            - Updated German, Korean, Romanian, and Ukrainian man page\n              translations.\n\n        * Added a few tests.\n\n### [`v5.4.6`](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/releases/tag/v5.4.6): XZ Utils 5.4.6 Stable\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/compare/v5.4.5...v5.4.6)\n\nHere is an extract from the NEWS file:\n\n    5.4.6 (2024-01-26)\n\n        * Fixed a bug involving internal function pointers in liblzma not\n          being initialized to NULL. The bug can only be triggered if\n          lzma_filters_update() is called on a LZMA1 encoder, so it does\n          not affect xz or any application known to us that uses liblzma.\n\n        * xz:\n\n            - Fixed a regression introduced in 5.4.2 that caused encoding\n              in the raw format to unnecessarily fail if --suffix was not\n              used. For instance, the following command no longer reports\n              that --suffix must be used:\n\n                  echo foo | xz --format=raw --lzma2 | wc -c\n\n            - Fixed an issue on MinGW-w64 builds that prevented reading\n              from or writing to non-terminal character devices like NUL.\n\n        * Added a new test.\n\n</details>\n\n<details>\n<summary>u-boot/u-boot (u-boot/u-boot)</summary>\n\n### [`v2024.04-rc1`](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.04-rc2...v2024.04-rc1)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.04-rc2...v2024.04-rc1)\n\n### [`v2024.04-rc2`](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.01-rc1...v2024.04-rc2)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.01-rc1...v2024.04-rc2)\n\n</details>\n\n---\n\n### Configuration\n\n📅 **Schedule**: Branch creation - At any time (no schedule defined), Automerge - At any time (no schedule defined).\n\n🚦 **Automerge**: Disabled by config. Full details are in the issue ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526)) and bug fix ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15571)).  There's also a developer's [bug summary](https://gist.github.com/rincebrain/e23b4a39aba3fadc04db18574d30dc73) that gives a good overview.  We recommend everyone either upgrade to 2.2.2 or 2.1.14 to get the fix.  The bug can cause data corruption due to an incorrect dirty dnode check.  This bug is very hard to hit, and really only came to light due to changes in `cp` in coreutils 9.x.  It's extremely unlikely that the bug was ever hit on EL7 or EL8, when running `cp` since they all use coreutils 8.x which performs file copies differently.\n\n*Updated (12/1/23):*\nEL9 was previously vulnerable since it uses coreutils 8.32 with the SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE patches backported from coreutils 9.x.\n\n-   FreeBSD: Fix ZFS so that snapshots under .zfs/snapshot are NFS visible [`v2.2.1`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/releases/tag/zfs-2.2.1)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/compare/zfs-2.2.0...zfs-2.2.1)\n\n##### Supported Platforms\n\n-   **Linux**: compatible with 3.10 - 6.6 kernels\n-   **FreeBSD**: compatible with releases starting from 12.2-RELEASE\n\n##### Changes\n\n**Note**:  We recommend that anyone running zfs-2.2.0 to please update to this release.  Gentoo users have identified a block cloning bug ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15526)) that can result in data corruption in zfs-2.2.0.  To workaround this, zfs-2.2.1 disables block cloning by default (see [https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15529](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15529) and [`479dca5`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/commit/479dca51c66a731e637bd2d4f9bba01a05f9ac9f)). Users running the 2.1.x branch or older are unaffected, as block cloning is a 2.2.x-only feature.\n\n-   ZTS: Fix 'could not unmount datasets' on Alma 9 ([https://github.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15542](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/pull/15542))\n-   zfs-2.2.1: Disable block cloning by default ([`479dca5`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/commit/479dca51c66a731e637bd2d4f9bba01a05f9ac9f))\n-   Add a tunable to disable BRT support. [#&#8203;15405](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15405)\n-   Fix ZED auto-replace for VDEVs using by-id paths [#&#8203;15363](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15363)\n-   Add zfs_prepare_disk script for disk firmware install [#&#8203;15243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15243)\n-   Large sync writes perform worse with slog [#&#8203;14378](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14378)\n-   FreeBSD: Improve taskq wrapper [#&#8203;15356](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15356)\n-   Fix block cloning between unencrypted and encrypted datasets [#&#8203;15464](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15464) [#&#8203;15465](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/15465)\n\n### [`v2.2.0`](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/releases/tag/zfs-2.2.0)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/compare/zfs-2.1.14...zfs-2.2.0)\n\n##### Supported Platforms\n\n-   **Linux**: compatible with 3.10 - 6.5 kernels\n-   **FreeBSD**: compatible with releases starting from 12.2-RELEASE\n\n##### New Features\n\n-   **Block cloning** ([#&#8203;13392](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13392)) - Block cloning is a facility that allows a file (or parts of a file) to be \"cloned\", that is, a shallow copy made where the existing data blocks are referenced rather than copied.  Later modifications to the data will cause a copy of the data block to be taken and that copy modified.  This facility is used to implement \"reflinks\" or \"file-level copy-on-write\".  Many common file copying programs, including newer versions of `/bin/cp` on Linux, will try to create clones automatically.\n\n-   **Linux container support** ([#&#8203;12209](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12209), [#&#8203;14070](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14070), [#&#8203;14097](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14097), [#&#8203;12263](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12263)) - Added support for Linux-specific container interfaces such as `renameat(2)`, support for overlayfs, idmapped mounts in a user namespace, and namespace delegation support for containers.\n\n-   **Scrub error log** ([#&#8203;12812](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12812), [#&#8203;12355](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12355)) - `zpool status` will report all filesystems, snapshots, and clones affected by a shared corrupt block.  `zpool scrub -e` can be used to scrub only the known damaged blocks in the error log to perform a fast, targeted repair when possible.\n\n-   **BLAKE3 checksums** ([#&#8203;12918](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12918)) - [BLAKE3](https://togithub.com/BLAKE3-team/BLAKE3) is a modern cryptographic hash algorithm focused on high performance.  It is much faster than sha256, sha512, and can be up 3x faster than Edon-R.  BLAKE3 is the recommended secure checksum.\n\n-   **Corrective \"zfs receive\"** ([#&#8203;9372](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/9372)) - A new type of `zfs receive` which can be used to heal corrupted data in filesystems, snapshots, and clones when a replica of the data already exists in the form of a backup send stream.\n\n-   **Vdev properties** ([#&#8203;11711](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11711)) - Provides observability of individual vdevs in a programmatic way.\n\n-   **Vdev and zpool user properties** ([#&#8203;11680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/11680)) - Lets you set custom user properties on vdevs and zpools, similar to the existing zfs dataset user properties.\n\n##### Performance\n\n-   **Fully adaptive ARC** ([#&#8203;14359](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14359)) - A unified ARC which relaxes the artificial limits imposed by both the MRU/MFU distribution and data/metadata distinction.  This allows the ARC to better adjust to highly dynamic workloads and minimizes the need for manual workload-dependent tuning.\n\n-   **SHA2 checksums** ([#&#8203;13741](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13741)) - Optimized SHA2 checksum implementation to use hardware acceleration when available.\n\n-   **Edon-R checksums** ([#&#8203;13618](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13618)) - Reworked the Edon-R variants and optimized the code to make several minor speed ups.\n\n-   **ZSTD early abort** ([#&#8203;13244](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13244)) - When using the zstd compression algorithm, data that can not be compressed is detected quickly, avoiding wasted work.\n\n-   **Prefetch improvements** ([#&#8203;14603](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14603), [#&#8203;14516](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14516), [#&#8203;14402](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14402), [#&#8203;14243](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14243), [#&#8203;13452](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13452)) - Extensive I/O prefetching analysis and optimization.\n\n-   **General optimization** ([#&#8203;14121](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14121), [#&#8203;14123](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14123), [#&#8203;14039](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14039), [#&#8203;13680](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13680), [#&#8203;13613](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13613), [#&#8203;13606](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13606), [#&#8203;13576](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13576), [#&#8203;13553](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/13553), [#&#8203;12789](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/12789), [#&#8203;14925](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14925), [#&#8203;14948](https://togithub.com/openzfs/zfs/issues/14948)) - Numerous performance improvements throughout.\n\n##### Additional Information\n\n-   **Documentation** - [OpenZFS documentation](https://openzfs.github.io/openzfs-docs/) for Linux and FreeBSD.\n\n-   **Change log** - [`v5.6.0`](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/releases/tag/v5.6.0): XZ Utils 5.6.0 Stable\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/compare/v5.4.6...v5.6.0)\n\nThere currently are no plans to maintain the 5.4.x branch, but releases\ncould be made if there is community interest.\n\nHere is an extract from the NEWS file:\n\n    5.6.0 (2024-02-24)\n\n        This bumps the minor version of liblzma because new features were\n        added. The API and ABI are still backward compatible with liblzma\n        5.4.x and 5.2.x and 5.0.x.\n\n        NOTE: As described in the NEWS for 5.5.2beta, the core components\n        are now under the BSD Zero Clause License (0BSD).\n\n        Since 5.5.2beta:\n\n        * liblzma:\n\n            - Disabled the branchless C variant in the LZMA decoder based\n              on the benchmark results from the community.\n\n            - Disabled x86-64 inline assembly on x32 to fix the build.\n\n        * Sandboxing support in xz:\n\n            - Landlock is now used even when xz needs to create files.\n              In this case the sandbox is has to be more permissive than\n              when no files need to be created. A similar thing was\n              already in use with pledge(2) since 5.3.4alpha.\n\n            - Landlock and pledge(2) are now stricter when reading from\n              more than one input file and only writing to standard output.\n\n            - Added support for Landlock ABI version 4.\n\n        * CMake:\n\n            - Default to -O2 instead of -O3 with CMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release.\n              -O3 is not useful for speed and makes the code larger.\n\n            - Now builds lzmainfo and lzmadec.\n\n            - xzdiff, xzgrep, xzless, xzmore, and their symlinks are now\n              installed. The scripts are also tested during \"make test\".\n\n            - Added translation support for xz, lzmainfo, and the\n              man pages.\n\n            - Applied the symbol versioning workaround for MicroBlaze that\n              is used in the Autotools build.\n\n            - The general XZ Utils and liblzma API documentation is now\n              installed.\n\n            - The CMake component names were changed a little and several\n              were added. liblzma_Runtime and liblzma_Development are\n              unchanged.\n\n            - Minimum required CMake version is now 3.14. However,\n              translation support is disabled with CMake versions\n              older than 3.20.\n\n            - The CMake-based build is now close to feature parity with the\n              Autotools-based build. Most importantly a few tests aren't\n              run yet. Testing the CMake-based build on different operating\n              systems would be welcome now. See the comment at the top of\n              CMakeLists.txt.\n\n        * Fixed a bug in the Autotools feature test for ARM64 CRC32\n          instruction support for old versions of Clang. This did not\n          affect the CMake build.\n\n        * Windows:\n\n            - The build instructions in INSTALL and windows/INSTALL*.txt\n              were revised completely.\n\n            - windows/build-with-cmake.bat along with the instructions\n              in windows/INSTALL-MinGW-w64_with_CMake.txt should make\n              it very easy to build liblzma.dll and xz.exe on Windows\n              using CMake and MinGW-w64 with either GCC or Clang/LLVM.\n\n            - windows/build.bash was updated. It now works on MSYS2 and\n              on GNU/Linux (cross-compiling) to create a .zip and .7z\n              package for 32-bit and 64-bit x86 using GCC + MinGW-w64.\n\n        * The TODO file is no longer installed as part of the\n          documentation. The file is out of date and does not reflect\n          the actual tasks that will be completed in the future.\n\n        * Translations:\n\n            - Translated lzmainfo man pages are now installed. These\n              had been forgotten in earlier versions.\n\n            - Updated Croatian, Esperanto, German, Hungarian, Korean,\n              Polish, Romanian, Spanish, Swedish, Vietnamese, and Ukrainian\n              translations.\n\n            - Updated German, Korean, Romanian, and Ukrainian man page\n              translations.\n\n        * Added a few tests.\n\n### [`v5.4.6`](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/releases/tag/v5.4.6): XZ Utils 5.4.6 Stable\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/tukaani-project/xz/compare/v5.4.5...v5.4.6)\n\nHere is an extract from the NEWS file:\n\n    5.4.6 (2024-01-26)\n\n        * Fixed a bug involving internal function pointers in liblzma not\n          being initialized to NULL. The bug can only be triggered if\n          lzma_filters_update() is called on a LZMA1 encoder, so it does\n          not affect xz or any application known to us that uses liblzma.\n\n        * xz:\n\n            - Fixed a regression introduced in 5.4.2 that caused encoding\n              in the raw format to unnecessarily fail if --suffix was not\n              used. For instance, the following command no longer reports\n              that --suffix must be used:\n\n                  echo foo | xz --format=raw --lzma2 | wc -c\n\n            - Fixed an issue on MinGW-w64 builds that prevented reading\n              from or writing to non-terminal character devices like NUL.\n\n        * Added a new test.\n\n</details>\n\n<details>\n<summary>u-boot/u-boot (u-boot/u-boot)</summary>\n\n### [`v2024.04-rc1`](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.04-rc2...v2024.04-rc1)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.04-rc2...v2024.04-rc1)\n\n### [`v2024.04-rc2`](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.01-rc1...v2024.04-rc2)\n\n[Compare Source](https://togithub.com/u-boot/u-boot/compare/v2024.01-rc1...v2024.04-rc2)\n\n</details>\n\n---\n\n### Configuration\n\n📅 **Schedule**: Branch creation - At any time (no schedule defined), Automerge - At any time (no schedule defined).\n\n🚦 **Automerge**: Disabled by config.
